  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a924bfb7-e4e0-47bb-a735-025c9a1f5df2'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

<span id="freeTextContainer14767800126925298705">In a discontent kingdom, civil war is brewing. To unify the divided people, Conner, a nobleman of the court, devises a cunning plan to find an impersonator of the king's long-lost son and install him as a puppet prince. Four orphans are recruited to compete for the role, including a defiant boy named Sage. Sage knows that Conner's motives are more than questionable, yet hi</span>
  <span id="freeText14767800126925298705" style="display:none">In a discontent kingdom, civil war is brewing. To unify the divided people, Conner, a nobleman of the court, devises a cunning plan to find an impersonator of the king's long-lost son and install him as a puppet prince. Four orphans are recruited to compete for the role, including a defiant boy named Sage. Sage knows that Conner's motives are more than questionable, yet his life balances on a sword's point—he must be chosen to play the prince or he will certainly be killed. But Sage's rivals have their own agendas as well.<br /><br />As Sage moves from a rundown orphanage to Conner's sumptuous palace, layer upon layer of treachery and deceit unfold, until finally, a truth is revealed that, in the end, may very well prove more dangerous than all of the lies taken together.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14767800126925298705" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

      </div>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_207789838" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/207789838" />
    <a title="Small Review" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4579690-small-review"><img alt="Small Review" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1291348460p2/4579690.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/207789838?book_show_action=true">Sep 12, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Small Review" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Small Review" href="/user/show/4579690-small-review">Small Review</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=g-fantasy">g-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=pages-300s">pages-300s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=library-own-print">library-own-print</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=2012-read">2012-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=library-own-re">library-own-re</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=special-shelf">special-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=library-own-rp">library-own-rp</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=library-own-read">library-own-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4579690-small-review?shelf=library-own-e">library-own-e</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer207789838" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6722426795583440246"><i>The False Prince</i> is <a href='http://smallreview.blogspot.com/p/definitions.html#thatbook' rel='nofollow noopener'>*THAT* book</a>! I stayed up way too late in order to finish it...and I'm seriously considering throwing all notion of a sleep schedule out the window and rereading the whole book right now. <br/><br/>Originally posted at <a href='http://smallreview.blogspot.com/2012/04/book-review-false-prince-by-jennifer.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Small Review</a><br/><br/><b>I call dibs on Sage <br/>(seriously ladies—don't underestimate me 'cause I'm small. I'll fight dirty.)</b><br/><br/>I knew this was going to be a Special Shelf book as soon as I "heard" Sage's voice narrating. Really, the story could have been downright awful (it isn't) and I st</span>
  <span id="freeText6722426795583440246" style="display:none"><i>The False Prince</i> is <a href="http://smallreview.blogspot.com/p/definitions.html#thatbook" rel="nofollow noopener">*THAT* book</a>! I stayed up way too late in order to finish it...and I'm seriously considering throwing all notion of a sleep schedule out the window and rereading the whole book right now. <br /><br />Originally posted at <a href="http://smallreview.blogspot.com/2012/04/book-review-false-prince-by-jennifer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Small Review</a><br /><br /><b>I call dibs on Sage <br />(seriously ladies—don't underestimate me 'cause I'm small. I'll fight dirty.)</b><br /><br />I knew this was going to be a Special Shelf book as soon as I "heard" Sage's voice narrating. Really, the story could have been downright awful (it isn't) and I still would have Special Shelved <i>The False Prince</i> on the strength of his voice alone. <br /><br />Sage embodies the personality of my number one most coveted male character type <i>ever</i> (yes, even over alpha men). The swoon is near uncontrollable. Luckily I was saved from being a total creeper lusting after a fifteen year old, because Sage's voice makes it very easy to imagine him as a completely adult 20 something. <br /><br />Sage is one of those characters who has Sherlock Holmes Superpowers of Observation and Fantasticness. Which is to say, he's always about ten steps ahead of everyone, can deduce master plans from a discarded gum wrapper, and pulls it all off with the type of suave demeanor that never fails to make my knees wobble. <br /><br />Plus, he's an underdog with attitude and I have a massive weakness for hot underdogs with swaggering attitude. Sage never seems to be able to resist needling those who lord over him, even if it means he'll get a bruise for his quip. He also lies like a pro, so that combined with his stealth and sneakiness make him the type of character that makes a great thief or conman. <br /><br />Basically, think Han Solo plus Sherlock Holmes' brains plus extra hotness and a smidgen of vulnerability and you've pretty much got Sage. <br /><br /><br /><b>Slow burn pacing </b><br /><br />As much as I love fast-paced books, my favorite kinds of books actually have a slow-burn pace (NOT to be confused with a <i>sloooow</i> pace, which is chock full of a lot of boring filler). In a slow-burn pace, plot details come together like a puzzle, with intrigue building steadily and keeping me on my toes throughout the whole book. Like a slow-burn romance, slow-burn pacing strings me along with delicious little morsels and makes me beg for more and more. <br /><br />The majority of <i>The False Prince</i> takes place in Conner's castle (the noble with The Plan) as he trains the boys and maliciously toys with their emotions (because, you see, only the guy that's picked to impersonate the prince gets to live). <br /><br />Backstabbing (literally!) and shaky alliances abound amid secrets, lies, and a truth you may or may not see coming but is so astoundingly great that surprise level doesn't even matter (I did guess the broad strokes early on, but the details were a surprise that darn near <i>broke my heart</i>). <br /><br />This is the first book in a series and it's very clear by the end of the book that there's a lot more to come in this story. Thankfully there isn't a dangling-by-your-fingertips cliffhanger, but it is very much like the end of <i>The Fellowship of the Ring</i> (the movie) where the first part of the quest is finished, the whole fellowship is broken, Frodo is poised to just walk into Mordor, and Aragorn is as hot as ever. <br /><br />So, yeah, I'm satisfied with everything I got and I can wait without suffering a heart attack because I know Sage is ok, but BIG STUFF is coming and I <i>cannot wait</i> to be a part of it! <br /><br /><br /><b>I can't NOT mention the romance</b><br /><br />The plot isn't the only thing set on slow burn. Yes, that's right! Slow-burn romance! But really, it's <i>very</i> slow burn because not much happens in this first book outside of lots of scenes with delicious tension. There's even a touch of, well, it's not quite hate-turned-love, but there's a little combativeness there and she isn't exactly falling all over herself to be with him (and, no, she isn't insane or blind, if you can believe it!). <br /><br />Really though, I'm not complaining <i>at all</i>. I'm firmly on the side that thinks it's much better to have the romance come together later on in the series. <br /><br /><br /><b>Bottom line</b><br /><br />I really...I can't...I just, I'm so unbelievably in love with <i>The False Prince</i> I don't even have the words to describe it. I'm so busy right now with packing and trying to get everything together to move in a few weeks, but I was very irresponsible because I pushed <i>everything</i> aside (including sleep AND food) just so I could devour this book.<br /><br />And then I went through serious mourning when I finished because of course there aren't any other books in the series yet and all of my other Special Shelf books are packed away. So I went back and reread all of my favorite scenes in <i>The False Prince</i>. And then all the other scenes. And then I read my favorite scenes again. And then I tried to read other books on my TBR but they're just not <i>The False Prince</i> and I think I'm going to cry I'm so desperate for more. <br /><br />Or, to put it in food terms, if I were given the choice between reading this book or attending an unlimited pastry banquet filled with every delectable treat imaginable, I would choose <i>The False Prince</i>—HANDS DOWN. <br /><br />I can think of no higher praise than that. <br /><br />5 Stars, Special Shelf<br /><br />Explanation of rating system: <a href="http://smallreview.blogspot.com/2010/11/star-rating-key.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Star Rating Key </a><br /><br /><br />Originally posted at <a href="http://smallreview.blogspot.com/2012/04/book-review-false-prince-by-jennifer.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Small Review</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362187695" rel="nofollow noopener">What did I think of the sequel, <i>The Runaway King</i>?</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6722426795583440246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_279679402" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/279679402" />
    <a title="Catie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1886642-catie"><img alt="Catie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1385169623p2/1886642.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/279679402?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Catie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Catie" href="/user/show/1886642-catie">Catie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=read-in-2012">read-in-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1886642-catie?shelf=audio">audio</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer279679402" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9270804529409648535">This book makes me want to put on my blandest Mr. Darcy voice and declare it “<i>tolerable…but not handsome enough to tempt me</i>.” This book is fine. I think many of you will notice its exercise-brightened eyes and charming irreverence and fall for it. But for me, it was just okay. <br/><br/>If you’ve read any amount of young adult fantasy, you probably know where this book is heading just from reading the synopsis – or hell, even the title! I had a lot of hope that this book would go in an unexpected directio</span>
  <span id="freeText9270804529409648535" style="display:none">This book makes me want to put on my blandest Mr. Darcy voice and declare it “<i>tolerable…but not handsome enough to tempt me</i>.” This book is fine. I think many of you will notice its exercise-brightened eyes and charming irreverence and fall for it. But for me, it was just okay. <br /><br />If you’ve read any amount of young adult fantasy, you probably know where this book is heading just from reading the synopsis – or hell, even the title! I had a lot of hope that this book would go in an unexpected direction or bring something new to the table, but it didn’t. Of course I had to stick around for the ending just to make sure but hopefully I can now save someone else the time. If you think you know where this book is going, you probably do.<br /><br />I have read other books (like <i>Finnikin of the Rock</i>) that had predictable outcomes as well, but that one at least had gorgeous writing, three dimensional characters, and impeccable world-building to keep me satisfied. This book had none of the above. My friend Tatiana recently used the term <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/283956289" rel="nofollow noopener">“fantasy lite”</a> in one of her reviews and I think this book fits that label perfectly. The world-building is very simplistic and barely deserves the title “fantasy”: a vaguely historical setting with almost no real culture, religion, or background. There is some small mention of a conflict with a few neighboring nations that is never developed. The main character is an argumentative, willful, scrappy boy who’s discovered in an orphanage by a man looking to train and install a look-alike as king (a puppet king, of course). He talks back, he pretends to be foolish, and of course he’s so much more than he appears to be. In summary: he’s Eugenides-lite.<br /><br />None of the other characters left more than surface impressions on me and I found it difficult to care about any of them. There is an attempt here at an unreliable first-person narrator that doesn’t quite succeed. Yes, Sage lies and pretends to be something he’s not, but the “little hints” about his true identity that are frequently dropped are so obvious that it’s hard not to get frustrated. And even his deception starts to feel illogical by the end. Why is he hiding who he is again? Why doesn’t he tell Mott? Or Imogen? Or Tobias? I can think of no reason except to possibly heighten the drama of his eventual reveal, which is so long in coming that I felt no excitement - only relief - when it finally came.<br /><br />Additionally, any intimacy that I felt with Sage’s point of view is effectively ruined by two sections of the book that are written in the third person. Why? I can think of nothing that is gained by showing us those two scenes in the third person. Yes, there is important action going on while the narrator is not present and yes, his entrance is supposed to be a big, climactic scene so in theory it might be nice to be able to see it as a member of the audience. But when you’ve committed the entire book to Sage’s point of view, it feels glaring and alienating to suddenly be thrust into a third person perspective. There are also a few scenes where Sage “checks out” for hours at a time. His narration is allowed convenient lapses so that he may go off and do secret-secret things without the reader knowing about it. It all feels as if the author didn’t quite know how to negotiate between an intimate first person narrator and the number of secrets that she wanted to keep from the reader. The end result is a very obvious, distanced, boring narrative.<br /><br />Wow. I thought that I was so-so about this book but apparently I disliked it more than I realized. I was originally thinking that even though I didn’t quite like it, it might still be a good recommendation for younger readers. But don’t young readers deserve to have great characters, world-building, and writing too? Why not read <i>Finnikin of the Rock, The Thief, Book of a Thousand Days, Graceling, Crown Duel</i>, or the many other well-written young adult fantasy novels instead?<br /><br />Also seen on <a href="http://www.thereadventurer.com/2/post/2012/04/ya-review-the-false-prince-by-jennifer-a-neilsen.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readventurer</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9270804529409648535" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1508649171" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508649171" />
    <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader"><img alt="Aj the Ravenous Reader" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1557800982p2/30248594.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1508649171?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aj the Ravenous Reader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aj the Ravenous Reader" href="/user/show/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader">Aj the Ravenous Reader</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Aj the Ravenous Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/10517119-pang">Pang</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30248594-aj-the-ravenous-reader?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508649171" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9554958704175440918"><br/><b>The following two paragraphs were going to be my review before I reached the turning point of the story:</b><br/><br/>In fairness to the book, I made this fatal mistake of reading another fantasy series after <i>Harry Potter</i> and poor book suffered from my biases. So to make it clear, had I read the book at a different time, I would have probably loved it but forgive me if for the entire reading all I could think about was how badly I miss <i>Harry Potter.</i><br/><br/>I do appreciate the short chapters and that overall, it was a</span>
  <span id="freeText9554958704175440918" style="display:none"><br /><b>The following two paragraphs were going to be my review before I reached the turning point of the story:</b><br /><br />In fairness to the book, I made this fatal mistake of reading another fantasy series after <i>Harry Potter</i> and poor book suffered from my biases. So to make it clear, had I read the book at a different time, I would have probably loved it but forgive me if for the entire reading all I could think about was how badly I miss <i>Harry Potter.</i><br /><br />I do appreciate the short chapters and that overall, it was a fast-paced fantasy read and that the premise (three orphan boys compete in order to be chosen as the false prince) was entertaining and engaging enough but this is one of those stories where I would honestly prefer a third person POV. I kind of felt weary of Sage’s (one of the orphan boys) voice and it kind of made the story predictable. I also thought Sage was not a very likable character. He’s too proud, ill-mannered and too full of himself. <br /><br /><b>Then came that most shocking climax</b><br /><br />And I had to eat all the previous words I wrote (except that I still badly miss HP and ultimately the reason I still settled for four stars). The revelation in this particular chapter felt like Hagrid (actually make that Graupy) backslapping my face leaving my two ginormous eyes unblinking, my mouth hanging open and temporarily incapable of speech. So let me just refer you to the rest of my friends’ amazing reviews. Take your pick!<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1355096396?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1”" rel="nofollow noopener">Sandra’s</a> (She actually badgered me about reading the book. Lol!) <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1542593199?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Masooma’s. </a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1508811255?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">my big sister’s</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1538188264?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Alafiya’s</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/984301930?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Ate Holly’s/Eilonwy’s</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409055516?book_show_action=true&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Nina’s</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1553237336?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Sarah’s</a><br /><br />And <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/397453249?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=2" rel="nofollow noopener">Pang’s</a><b> who also happens to be celebrating her birthday TODAY! Happy Birthday, my charming, sweet friend! Celebrate your special day the best way you can! BE HAPPY! &lt;3 </b><br /><br /></span>

  <span id="freeText11207767356641205786" style="display:none"><blockquote><b>Since there are quite a number of similarities of both plot and characters, I can't help but compare <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12432220.The_False_Prince__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___1_" title="The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, #1) by Jennifer A.     </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1854142286" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6624499180257704337"><a href='http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><a href='https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Instagram</a> || <a href='https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell' rel='nofollow noopener'>Twitter</a> || <a href='https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Facebook</a> || <a href='http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> || <a href='https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pinterest</a><br/><br/><br/>Carthya is a kingdom on the brink of war. The royal family is dead. The youngest son, Jaron, is missing, presumed dead. A group of regents all have their eye on the vacant throne, and if one of them seizes power, it's likely that the entire kingdom will be plunged into ruin. But one nobleman named Conner has a plan. He's rounded up a group of four orphan boys - Latamer, Roden, Tobias, and Sage - that all have the look of Jaron. His plan </span>
  <span id="freeText6624499180257704337" style="display:none"><a href="http://readasaurus.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1459070464i/18565492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="https://www.instagram.com/neniagram/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> || <a href="https://twitter.com/NeniaCampbell" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> || <a href="https://www.facebook.com/aficionenias/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> || <a href="http://www.amazon.com/Nenia-Campbell/e/B00AWVRKMS" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> || <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/mightbeamisprin/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a><br><br><br>Carthya is a kingdom on the brink of war. The royal family is dead. The youngest son, Jaron, is missing, presumed dead. A group of regents all have their eye on the vacant throne, and if one of them seizes power, it's likely that the entire kingdom will be plunged into ruin. But one nobleman named Conner has a plan. He's rounded up a group of four orphan boys - Latamer, Roden, Tobias, and Sage - that all have the look of Jaron. His plan is to groom them, train them, and in two weeks, crown the one who has best taken to the role. As for the others, well...<i>death</i>.<br><br><br><br>Despite being a thief and an orphan, Sage is a proud boy, and doesn't take kindly to Conner's cruel tyranny. He sustains a number of beatings, whippings, and torments at the hands of his captor. The other boys can't be trusted, either. They're all in competition for the same thing, and if one of them fails, the survivors in this cruel competition will gain from their loss. <br><br><br><br>THE FALSE PRINCE is one of those books that sounded so good, I was afraid to read it, because I couldn't stand the thought of being disappointed. This was in error. THE FALSE PRINCE is awesome. It's got all the things I love in YA - court intrigue, surprising twists, peril, death, heartbreak, friendship, competitions, deception, and action. Sage is an excellent narrator. He has all the snark of Artemis Fowl, but the humanity and determination of characters like Katniss Everdeen that make your heart ache for them as well. No matter how big a jerk he is, there's never a moment where you don't want him to succeed, because you feel in your heart that he deserves it.<br><br><br><br>The only things that I can really ding this book for are - the main twist. I saw it coming pretty early on. Also, Roden's and Tobias's characters started to feel pretty interchangeable in the last third of the book. Roden especially did some things that just felt out of character. This is just me being nit-picky, though. I finished this book in a single sitting; it was just that good.<br><br><br><br>Lord, I need that sequel. That <i>ending</i>.<br><br><br><br>5 stars</span>

<div id="review_888182994" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/888182994" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/888182994?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=loanable-kindle-books">loanable-kindle-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=princes-and-princesses">princes-and-princesses</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer888182994" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14521703901928254134">3.5 stars. Fourteen year old Sage is involuntarily hauled out of a rough orphanage by Bevin Conner nobleman in their kingdom of Carthya, as part of Conner's secret and treasonous plan (though ostensibly and debatably he has the ultimate good of the kingdom at heart): train a group of four (very soon three) orphans with the skills they would have as young nobleman, and pick the best one to impersonate the king's younger son Jaron, who was lost at sea four years earlier, at the age of ten. Once hi</span>
  <span id="freeText14521703901928254134" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Fourteen year old Sage is involuntarily hauled out of a rough orphanage by Bevin Conner nobleman in their kingdom of Carthya, as part of Conner's secret and treasonous plan (though ostensibly and debatably he has the ultimate good of the kingdom at heart): train a group of four (very soon three) orphans with the skills they would have as young nobleman, and pick the best one to impersonate the king's younger son Jaron, who was lost at sea four years earlier, at the age of ten. Once his choice is installed in the royal family, Conner will be able to control the kingdom through this boy. <br /><br />The group embarks on an intense two-week period of tutoring and training, with a constant life-and-death battle between the boys to win ... since they suspect, with very good reason, that the losers will be killed to protect the secrecy of the plan. But Sage can't resist rebelling against Conner, in both small and large ways.<br /><br /><i>The False Prince</i> is generally well written for a YA book and kept my interest, but I was irritated by several details:<br /><br />- Sage's constant mouthing off. I get enough teenage lip IRL, I don't need to read a book full of it.<br /><br />- insufficient world-building. It seemed like it was a general European-ish 18th or 19th century-ish kingdom. There was no magic that I recall, so I'm not sure why the author created make-believe countries without bothering to flesh them out.<br /><br />- Two weeks (!!) is all that Conner takes to turn three rag-tag orphans into literate, knowledgeable, sword-wielding, horse-riding princes? Not a chance. You'd need six months, maybe a year, at least. (Shannon Hale's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/85990.Princess_Academy__Princess_Academy___1_" title="Princess Academy (Princess Academy, #1) by Shannon Hale" rel="nofollow noopener">Princess Academy</a> got this detail much better.)<br /><br />- Very spoilerish reason here: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[What king (supposedly a loving father) would have his 10 year old son spend several years fending for himself in an inadequate, hostile orphanage, with almost no supervision or protection? He would send him to some trusted friend--he MUST have had at least one trusted friend--preferably outside of the country, where he could grow up safe and cared for. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />I did appreciate <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[the similarities to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> and the twist, though I saw it coming. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I liked <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> much better personally, but I think this book is more accessible for younger readers. I'll pass this on to my 12 year old son, who will probably love it. <br /><br />Edited to add: my son reported that he's already read this book and that it was, and I quote, "awesome." So there you go.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14521703901928254134" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1542593199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1542593199" />
    <a title="Masooma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26677122-masooma"><img alt="Masooma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1455366226p2/26677122.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1542593199?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Masooma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Masooma" href="/user/show/26677122-masooma">Masooma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Masooma by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/36574090-muse-ic">Muse-ic ♬</a>
  </div>


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1542593199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3601619071653395086">Sick Latamer, hot-headed Sage, erudite Tobias and strong Roden have one thing in common- a physical similarity to the 4-year lost and probably dead Prince Jaron of the Kingdom of Carthya. With the poisoned death of the royal family, the kingdom is at the brink of an upheaval and the so-called patriot nobleman Conner sees this as a perfect opportunity to bring forward the lost Prince. Thus, it all comes down to the frail shoulders of 15 year old orphans who are literally in a do or die situation.</span>
  <span id="freeText3601619071653395086" style="display:none">Sick Latamer, hot-headed Sage, erudite Tobias and strong Roden have one thing in common- a physical similarity to the 4-year lost and probably dead Prince Jaron of the Kingdom of Carthya. With the poisoned death of the royal family, the kingdom is at the brink of an upheaval and the so-called patriot nobleman Conner sees this as a perfect opportunity to bring forward the lost Prince. Thus, it all comes down to the frail shoulders of 15 year old orphans who are literally in a do or die situation. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12432220.The_False_Prince__The_Ascendance_Trilogy___1_" title="The False Prince (The Ascendance Trilogy, #1) by Jennifer A. Nielsen" rel="nofollow noopener">The False Prince</a> is, in one word, BRILLIANT. To me, there were hardly any faults to point fingers at. The writing is perfect and the description is crystal clear to take you to the training of these competitors, introducing to you the history of Carthya, the royal hierarchy, the fun of sword-fighting, horse-riding and the customs and culture of the realm. <br />The chief aspect of Jennifer's writing is, however, the dialogues. <b>Crispy and witty, the dialogues paired with a piquant voice of the narrator, Sage keeps one fully engulfed in the novel.</b><br /><br />Now you maybe thinking that this book is perhaps a simple, straight-forward read to the sabotage of the throne after the imposter Prince's training. But let me ensure you the plot is anything but that. The difficult and adamant working of Sage's mind is one feature which keeps the novel from sinking into just simple training. There is one master twist awaiting to welcome you as well. <b>And the best part is that this twist could’ve easily made the novel a boring, predictable read but fear not. The author sure knows how to develop and play with her readers' interests.</b><br /><br /><b>In addition to the perfect writing, a world built with a realistic infrastructure and an amazing plot twist, there is one other treat viz; a strong, appealing central character. </b><br /><br /><b>Sage has a madcap, stubborn, and sharp-witted voice.</b> His powerful narration had me hooked to the book from the first page itself and I wanted to know what or how he would respond in the very next second. He is definitely one of the best characters I've ever known. Take a peak yourself:<br /><br /><i>Once in a conversation with Mrs. Turbeldy, I compared myself to a caterpillar that went wherever I wanted with barely any notice. She compared me to a cockroach instead, who ran about freely in the darkness and scattered in the light. It was meant as an insult, but I thought it was a fair comparison, even a compliment judging by how hard they are to catch.</i><br /><br />All other characters are masterfully created. I had only a teensy bit issue with the ladies- Imogen and Amarinda but I'm ready to overlook their average roles because in the grand scheme of the awesomeness of this novel it doesn't really count. <br /><br />Lastly,<b> the book has little to do with romance.</b> It majorly focuses on a strong protagonist guaranteed to make this novel one helluva ride for you. <br /><br /><b>Layered with intrigue, competition, adventure, adrenaline, whip-smart dialogues, a refreshing voice and smart, forward planning the book isn't one which you should leave into the ignoring hallows. </b><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="3601619071653395086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_223434721" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/223434721" />
    <a title="Experiment BL626" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626"><img alt="Experiment BL626" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335917426p2/4582872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/223434721?book_show_action=true">Oct 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Experiment BL626" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Experiment BL626" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626">Experiment BL626</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13561824-the-false-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer223434721" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18335297193415392879">CAUTION: Long Review, Slight Spoilers<br/><br/>Feeble Latamer. Boastful Roden. Bookish Tobias. Defiant Sage. Four boys. One throne. Who will become <s>America's Next Top Model</s> Carthya's Next Reigning King? In ANTM the reality TV show, the contestants choose to participate and if they lose then they are sent home. In <i>The False Prince</i>, the contestants are coerced to participate and if they lose then they are sentenced to death. At the end, there will be only one one winner, one survivor.<br/><br/><i>The False Prince</i> is tol</span>
  <span id="freeText18335297193415392879" style="display:none">CAUTION: Long Review, Slight Spoilers<br /><br />Feeble Latamer. Boastful Roden. Bookish Tobias. Defiant Sage. Four boys. One throne. Who will become <s>America's Next Top Model</s> Carthya's Next Reigning King? In ANTM the reality TV show, the contestants choose to participate and if they lose then they are sent home. In <i>The False Prince</i>, the contestants are coerced to participate and if they lose then they are sentenced to death. At the end, there will be only one one winner, one survivor.<br /><br /><i>The False Prince</i> is told from Sage's side in 1st PoV as he try to survive a mad nobleman's plan to usurp the throne. The king, the queen, and the crown prince are dead. The youngest son of the royal family Jaron is lost and presumed to be dead... Or is he? The four boys coerced by Conner all look physically similar to Jaron. The winner will become the imposter puppet prince.<br /><br />TFP starts off with Conner and his two henchmen, Mott and Cregan, kidnapping Sage. When Sage wakes up, he soon encounter the other orphans. Right off in chapter 3, one of the orphans gets killed — the feeble Latamer. With this quick cruel act, the story pushes the following points: 1) Conner is ruthless. 2) This is serious business. 3) There is no escape. 4) Every orphan for himself. And 5) Only one boy will survive.<br /><br />Thus begins a tale of treason and treachery with an approximate word count of 77,000.<blockquote>“You’re a trick to figure out, Sage. Would you ever be on my side, even if I chose you above the other boys?”<br /><br />“I’m only on my side. Your trick will be convincing me that helping you helps me.”<br /><br />“What if I did?” Conner asked. “How far would you go to win?”<br /> <br />“The better question, sir, is how far you will go to win.” I looked him steadily in the eyes as I spoke, although his back was to the fire and his eyes were set in shadow. “You killed Latamer. So we know you’re willing to murder to win.”<br /> <br />“I am.” Conner backed up, speaking to all of us again. “And I’m willing to lie, to cheat, and to steal. I’m willing to commend my soul to the devils if necessary because I believe there is exoneration in my cause. I need one of you to conduct the greatest fraud ever perpetrated within the country of Carthya. This is a lifetime commitment. It will never be safe to back down from my plan and tell the truth. To do so would destroy not only you but the entire country. And you will do it to save Carthya.”</blockquote><b>The Characters</b><br /><br />+++ Sage the defiant orphan, our hero<br /><br />A thief. A liar. From start to finish, Sage was one of the best characters I have read about. One of the criteria for me to 5-stars rate a book is that the book must have a kick-ass protagonist. Sage was a kick-ass protagonist.<br /><br />Sage's biggest flaw, beside being a thief and a liar, is that his cleverness sometime slips into foolishness of the life-or-death kinds. Yet for all his shortcomings, he care for the downtrodden, keep his promises, and kill only in self-defense. There was never a moment when my sympathy for Sage slipped, never a moment when I got irritated by him either. Sage is well aware of the defects in his character and quick to realize the consequences of his action. He deals with them, he get things done, he survive.<br /><br />Sage acted convincingly as a poor orphan. Who have time to mope and moan about the disadvantages about one's life and the unfairness of it all when you're too busy trying to survive. Sage doesn't mope. He may worry. He may regret. He may make mistakes, get into <i>more</i> life-threatening situations, and bitch about them. But he never mope. He survive.<br /><br />+++ Conner the ruthless noble, our villain<br /><br />Conner is what we in the modern world would call a terrorist. He says his plan will save the kingdom, that what he doing is patriotic. He says he doesn't want the throne itself, that he just wants a prince who will become a king that will listen to his ever so wise advice. He says the death of three young orphans is regrettable, but the surviving one will help him save the kingdom!<br /><br />I hate Conner because he's the villain, he's the reason for our hero's predicament. He fucking killed poor Latamer! But I also love Conner because he was deliciously ruthless and mad. Sage and Conner shared several traits such as a skill for scheming, but the biggest thing that separated them was genuine empathy. Empathy for your fellow humans. Sage has that, Conner doesn't. Despite whatever BS Conner spout, his action speak the loudest and it says he is self-serving and delusional.<br /><br />+++ Tobias and Roden the other orphans, our hero's rivals<br /><br />It would have too easy to typecast Tobias as the brainy but bashful orphan and Roden as the brawny but butt-headed orphan, but the story didn't. Tobias and Roden tried their best to out-scheme Sage and each other. All the boys knew each other's talent and knew well that there wasn't a chance to outperform their rivals' talent so they relied on psychological warfare. Our hero, Sage, may be the cleverest of them all but he is human and he cannot be cleverer than the others all the time.<br /><br />+++ Imogen and Amarinda, our hero's potential love interests<br /><br />I say <i>potential</i> love interests because in TFP neither girls liked Sage in that way. I even hesitate to say they are love interests because their role was relatively small — they were supporting characters. Plus, I believe the reason Sage paid attention to these girls because he couldn't look away from a person in hurt.<br /><br />Imogen is a mute servant oppressed in Conner's castle, while Amarinda is a foreign princess betrothed to whoever becomes the king of Carthya. First impression says they are damsels in distress, but upon a further look I saw they were strong-willed. These girls didn't ask for help, they didn't need Sage to save them from their circumstance. Whatever had happened, they chose to tough it out. These girls don't want pity. What they do want is honesty, because both hate to be deceived, even for the best of intention. At TFP's end, both girls are finding it a very hard time to forgive Sage.<br /><br />Anyway, I'm not sure if there will be a love triangle. My interpretation is that Sage see Imogen as a fellow downtrodden to be rescued. Amarinda, on the other hand, loved the crown prince, Darius. There were no flirting or kissing in this novel, thus no romance. If anything, I think adding romance would have weakened the plot and distracted Sage's goal to survive.<br /><br /><b>The Writing</b><br /><br />The story was minimal on imagery and world-building, but I saw that as good things. TFP prefer the reader to learn about its world through dialogue and action. There were no info-dumping. If there was, then it would probably be the flashback that occurred in two consecutive chapters towards the end. Two consecutive chapters of a flashback may seem long in saying it as so, but I devoured these chapters quickly. They weren't long to me as a reader who generally dislike flashbacks. Basically, the novel was character-driven. Most of it took place at Conner's castle where the orphans learn how to act as Jaron.<br /><br />The pacing was steady, but there was always a sense of urgency and danger underlining it. There were no slow moments for me because I was entirely captivated by the novel. The writing was straightforward, no purplish prose or corny lines. Well, maybe a few corny lines.<br /><br /><b>Twists and Turns</b><br /><br />Slightly predictable, YMMV. There were hints found around so I got ecstatic in figuring things out before the story revealed its secrets to me. I didn't expect all the twists and turns, a few I didn't expect them to happen immediately in this novel. TFP hardly left any loose ends; there is no cliffhanger. Nevertheless, I'm dying to read the sequel because TFP ended on such a high note. <br /><br /><b>Conclusion</b><br /><br />I rate TFP 5-stars for it was amazing. TFP is a popcorn fantasy. I had great joy in watching Sage maneuvering and manipulating his way around. The climax in chapter 53 was The Bomb. I kept reading it over and over again.<br /><br />I recommend it for anyone who enjoys <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/22542.Megan_Whalen_Turner" title="Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">Megan Whalen Turner</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/448873.The_Thief__The_Queen_s_Thief___1_" title="The Thief (The Queen's Thief, #1) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen's Thief series</a>. TFP is what book 4 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6527841.A_Conspiracy_of_Kings__The_Queen_s_Thief___4_" title="A Conspiracy of Kings (The Queen's Thief, #4) by Megan Whalen Turner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Conspiracy of Kings</a> should have been imo.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18335297193415392879" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer14503517112354892709"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br/><br/>WHAT THE SWEET HELL WAS THIS. <br/><br/>I went into this book with absolutely no expectations (thank you, inexistent hype) and came out gasping and fangirling and hyperventilating, which is the absolute best way to experience a book. <br/><br/><u>The three pillars of <i>The False Prince</i></u><br/>♖ In my opinion, <b>the main character, Sage, is this book's strongest asset.</b> He thieves and rebels. He's intelligent and feisty but kind-hearted. And he's a bomb of reckless plans, snappy retorts and defiance ready to detonate. <b>In s</b></span>
  <span id="freeText14503517112354892709" style="display:none"><b>4.5 STARS</b><br /><br />WHAT THE SWEET HELL WAS THIS. <br /><br />I went into this book with absolutely no expectations (thank you, inexistent hype) and came out gasping and fangirling and hyperventilating, which is the absolute best way to experience a book. <br /><br /><u>The three pillars of <i>The False Prince</i></u><br />♖ In my opinion, <b>the main character, Sage, is this book's strongest asset.</b> He thieves and rebels. He's intelligent and feisty but kind-hearted. And he's a bomb of reckless plans, snappy retorts and defiance ready to detonate. <b>In short, he's pretty damn swoon-worthy.</b> To be frank here, the book would've been only half as good without Sage to wreak havoc. <b>I further liked the characterization of the supporting characters.</b> Latamer is the sickly one and serves as a tool. Roden (or RodenT, as Masooma and I like to call him) is described as a muscle-packed boy with tanned skin – in other words, <b>he's the do-er.</b> Tobias is a skinny boy with a brain full of history facts – <b>he's the thinker.</b> And, well, Sage is both. <br />♖ The <b>plot was unspectacular for the most part</b> but it didn't bother me in the slightest because, as I said, Sage kept me entertained enough. What really gripped me regarding the plot were its twists: <b>The plot twists were mind-blowing.</b> Yes, I did have an idea as to how the story could turn out. And yes, I threw them all over board because I thought I was wrong. This kind of plotting actually reminded me a bit of <i>The Kiss of Deception</i>, only backwards. <br />♖ The third pillar consists of little things I cherish about this book: <b>The soft touch of a slow-burn romance, the tug-of-war between Sage and Conner, and the loyalty of what's-his-name</b> (see, Nina? This is why we don't write a review 1 month after having read the book). <br /><br />Speaking of writing this review: If my friend Chantal hadn't picked up this book, I would've never realized that I still had a review to write for this. #massivefailure<br /><br />You don't want to pick up this book for the action, the swordfights and the courtfights. Because, even though some aspects are there, they are not the core of this book. <b>You want to pick up this book for Sage because he's one of a damn kind.</b> <br /><br />Also, I think celebrations are in order: This was <b>book #330</b> on my read-shelf *fistbumps air*<br /><br /></span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10249396496126803568">HOLLA! JUST AS AMAZING THE SECOND TIME AROUND. Except possibly even better because now I know what details to look for. The experience was so much more vivid. Anyone who's read this knows EXACTLY what I'm talking about. <br/><b>If you haven't read this, then prepare yourself for a recommendation comin' atchu!</b><br/> The following is my old review. Spoilers are 100% marked. It's a fangirly review. Read it!<br/>___________________________________________________________<br/>Congratulations book! You just earned yourself a</span>
  <span id="freeText10249396496126803568" style="display:none">HOLLA! JUST AS AMAZING THE SECOND TIME AROUND. Except possibly even better because now I know what details to look for. The experience was so much more vivid. Anyone who's read this knows EXACTLY what I'm talking about. <br><b>If you haven't read this, then prepare yourself for a recommendation comin' atchu!</b><br> The following is my old review. Spoilers are 100% marked. It's a fangirly review. Read it!<br>___________________________________________________________<br>Congratulations book! You just earned yourself a position on <b>
  <u>the honorary Favorites Shelf</u>
</b>!<br><br>This is a SOLID 5 STAR READ! Usually when I give a book 5 stars, I'll think about it beforehand and wonder if the book really deserved 5 stars.<br>With <i>The False Prince</i> though, there was <b>
  <u>no doubt in my mind that this book deserved beyond 5 shining stars</u>
</b>!<br><br>I would recommend this to everyone. EVERYONE!! I sent many of you this book as a recommendation. Trust me when I say that this book is the embodiment of the word "fabulous". I am so deeply in love with it!<br><br>I will not cover this review with an epic spoiler alert, though there will be spoilers! Don't worry though, I will mark them.<br><b>*SERIOUSLY, IF YOU HAVE NOT READ THIS BOOK, DO NOT OPEN THE SPOILERS!</b> You will ruin it for yourself. Completely and utterly ruin it. Don't do it.<br><br>You've been warned!<br><br>In the kingdom of Carthya, a civil war is brewing. Discontent and anger is spreading through the land, and it's the King and royal family's job to quell the unrest.......right??<br>There is one tiny problem with that plan. <b>There is no royal family.</b> That's right! They're <i>dead</i>. The King, Queen, and their son Darius are DEAD!<br>And the people are unaware. There are rumors, but the people haven't confirmed them. It's only a matter of time before the people demand a replacement. They need a king on the throne. <br><br>Cue Conner, a nobleman of the court. Conner's plan is to resurrect Prince Jaron, the youngest son of the royal family who was said to have been killed/drowned in a pirate attack on his ship four years earlier. The prince's body was never found, so Conner's goal is to use that shred of doubt to say that Prince Jaron was actually alive and place him on the throne. The only problem is that Conner is absolutely sure that the prince is dead. So what now?<br><br>Conner scours the orphanages of Carthya and gathers four boys who have a physical resemblance to the late Prince.<br><b>Meet Latamer, Roden, Tobias, and Sage.</b><br>Each boy has his own memorable qualities. Latamer is feeble, Tobias is educated, Roden is strong, and Sage is snarky and stubborn. <br>After two weeks of different types of training, Conner would select the most suited boy to present to the royal court as the faux Prince Jaron.<br>Our protagonist is Sage, a boy who is originally from one of the neighboring kingdoms. <br><br><br>I love Sage! He's the epitome of awesome boy characters. I love his attitude, I love his personality, I love him! He kind of reminds me of a more mature Percy Jackson. <br>I love how kind he is to the servants and how he stands up to Conner.<br><br>I loved how there was virtually no romance in this book! Sure, Sage had his fondness for a certain character, and that developed nicely. Actually, I see potential of a love triangle in the next book, but a <b>juicy and well-placed love triangle</b>, not a crappy one.<br><br>Imogen, one of Conner's servants, is awesome! <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[She pretends to be a mute to direct Conner's attention away from her. No body knows that she truly can speak, save for Sage. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I also really liked how Princess Amarinda, Darius' betrothed, was not a bratty girl. I truly admired her personality!<br><br>I DESPISE Cregan!! Hate him.<br>I love Mott because he's truly a kind-hearted man and guided Sage whenever he could.<br><br>My opinion of the other boys changed throughout the book:<br>I had nothing against them at first.....then Tobias was all like "I'm gonna be prince so don't try to get in my way" and he tried to hurt Sage and I was like GTFO (maybe you saw my status update about that?) And then the <i>minute</i> he got in trouble, he begged Sage for mercy. Sage, being the awesome person he is, agreed to protect him and stuff as long as Tobias swore loyalty to him. Tobias proved to be useful later, so I half forgave him.<br>Roden was mostly meh, but I <i>really</i> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[hated <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> him in the end!<br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1448308574i/17120626.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>
  <u>***REMINDER: Do not open the spoiler if you haven't read this!</u>
</b><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So let's talk about this "Sage is actually Jaron" thing. OMG!!!!! My jaw literally dropped when I connected the dots! Even though this book was in first person, with some <b>artfully placed ambiguity and unnoticeable skirting around the topic</b>, the author completely avoided the subject until Conner chooses Sage--Sorry--<i>Jaron</i> as his prince. AAAAAAHHHHHHHH! And stupid Conner is actually the one who hired the pirates from Avenia to kill Jaron and is the one that freaking killed his family to eventually become king, that stupid jerk! <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1452800547ra/17745636.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Jaron is so smart! It's amazing how, once you find out the truth, you look back at seemingly unimportant previous events in a whole new light! The coin flip? The fool's gold rock? The left-handedness? HIS STRIKING RESEMBLANCE TO THE PRINCE?! Or should I say, to himself? Really, you wonder how you didn't figure it out before, when it should have been obvious! The "False Prince" isn't so false after all! <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><i>The False Prince</i> is a book that deserves a place on everyone's shelf! Add it if you have not! You will not regret it!!<br>I cannot express enough how much I loved this! It was also amazing as an audiobook; the narrator was fantastic :D<br>As I approached the end, I was jumping around the house, shaking my brother by the shoulders, and telling him that he just <i>has</i> to read this book!<br>Simply AH-MAZING! AMAZING FABULOUS COOL FANTASTIC FUN QUICK-PACED READ IT NOW!<br>You're welcome!</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_351701943" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/351701943" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/351701943?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/13561824-the-false-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=middle-grade">middle-grade</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=half-fantasy">half-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=buddy-reads-are-the-best">buddy-reads-are-the-best</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer351701943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12712651649385101668"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2015/09/review-the-false-prince-by-jennifer-a-nielsen-jessicadhaluska-nielsenwriter-scholastic.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>THE FALSE PRINCE by Jennifer Nielsen is in my opinion exactly what juvenile fiction/middle grade fantasy is supposed to be.<br/><br/>Nimble-fingered orphans who proactively take measures to fill their bellies? Check.<br/><br/>Evil masterminds plotting to overthrow a kingdom? Also, check.<br/><br/>A Big Secret that isn't easily identifiable b/c super sneaky use of ambiguity? CHECK.<br/><br/>And all of that is in addition to the highly entertaining snark that does not stop. <------SNARK, I love it.<br/><br/>Meet Sage.<br/><br/>Sage </span>
  <span id="freeText12712651649385101668" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2015/09/review-the-false-prince-by-jennifer-a-nielsen-jessicadhaluska-nielsenwriter-scholastic.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>THE FALSE PRINCE by Jennifer Nielsen is in my opinion exactly what juvenile fiction/middle grade fantasy is supposed to be.<br><br>Nimble-fingered orphans who proactively take measures to fill their bellies? Check.<br><br>Evil masterminds plotting to overthrow a kingdom? Also, check.<br><br>A Big Secret that isn't easily identifiable b/c super sneaky use of ambiguity? CHECK.<br><br>And all of that is in addition to the highly entertaining snark that does not stop. &lt;------SNARK, I love it.<br><br>Meet Sage.<br><br>Sage is all things cocky and self-assured that make up clever early adolescent boys. He can steal whatever he needs without getting caught, and if he <i>is</i> caught, no one can hold on to him long enough to prove it.<br><br>He's not happy with his lot in life, but he understands his place in the world and is content to live day-to-day without giving much thought to what he'll do when he's forced to leave the home for boys where he currently resides when he turns fifteen.<br><br>Meet Conner.<br><br>Conner is a nobleman on a mission to Save the Kingdom. A mission that involves rounding up orphan boys of a certain age and appearance and training them to behave convincingly like noblemen themselves.<br><br>Sage wants nothing to do with whatever Conner's plan is, but when it becomes obvious that he must submit or be hunted and silenced, he decides to stick around and see what all of this is really about.<br><br>If <i>you</i> want to know what it's all about, you'll have to read it for yourself (b/c not telling).<br><br>And I hope you do. Not only is it a quick, easy read, but this is the kind of book that parents can read out loud to their children, children can read to themselves, or adults can read for their own pleasure.<br><br>Is the world-building or plot as complicated or as twisty as an adult fantasy novel? No. It's not. J-U-V-E-N-I-L-E fiction. But the story and characters are more than interesting enough to keep you entertained, especially if you don't go into reading it with unrealistic expectations.<br><br>At least I think it is. And this is the second time I've read it, so not a fluke. Highly recommended.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12712651649385101668" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1312416946" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1312416946" />
    <a title="Simona B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b"><img alt="Simona B" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408893128p2/5312173.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1312416946?book_show_action=true">Jun 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Simona B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Simona B" href="/user/show/5312173-simona-b">Simona B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780545284141" href="/book/show/15815401-the-false-prince">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=2000">2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5312173-simona-b?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1312416946" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18181346252962882596"><b>"If we can weed out your bad manners and defiant nature, I suspect you could convince the nobles that you are him."<br/>"If you weed those out, then there's nothing left of me."</b><br/><br/>In the interests of the future readers: I'm nearing the end of <i>The Runaway King</i> now, the second book in the <b>trilogy</b>, and as far as I can tell so far, <i>The False Prince</i> works perfectly, probably even better, as a <b>standalone</b>. Therefore, if you'd like to give this world a chance but you're not sure you want to go through all three</span>
  <span id="freeText18181346252962882596" style="display:none"><b>"If we can weed out your bad manners and defiant nature, I suspect you could convince the nobles that you are him."<br />"If you weed those out, then there's nothing left of me."</b><br /><br />In the interests of the future readers: I'm nearing the end of <i>The Runaway King</i> now, the second book in the <b>trilogy</b>, and as far as I can tell so far, <i>The False Prince</i> works perfectly, probably even better, as a <b>standalone</b>. Therefore, if you'd like to give this world a chance but you're not sure you want to go through all three books, in my opinion you can safely read the first and stop there. This doesn not alter the fact that I'm finding the second installment as entertaining at the first, but generally not as good.<br /><br />•<b>Sage<a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[/Jaron <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></b> is a stunningly <b>compelling</b> lead. He's barely fifteen, but he has the mind of the most seasoned -and charming- outlaw. He is <b>cunning</b>, <b>sharp-tongued</b>, the type who makes sure to have not only a backup plan, but a backup plan for the backup plan and so on, as far as his wits can go. He's also the type who lets you think you should keep an eye on your watch while he steals your wallet, and that can cheat and lie to your face without you noticing until it's already too late. His backstory may not shine for its originality, but it's unexpected and even cruel, and it only made me love him more. He alone suffices to earn the book all the stars.<br /><br />•<b>The plot twist</b>: okay, maybe it's a bit far-fetched to call it so because honestly, who wasn't imagining it? But when it's <b>predictable</b> and you <b>enjoy it nonetheless</b>, isn't that almost as good as when you don't expect it at all? So, yes, no complaints from me on that matter. <br /><br />•I admit that <b>the first half</b> of the book is no more than <b>mediocre</b>, though not boring nor badly written and still absolutely enjoyable. From approximately the middle onwards, it only gets better and better, becoming a true <b>page-turner</b>.<br /><br />•<b>The secondary characters</b> do their job just fine, but without particular brightness. At times, I'm afraid I found them blander than I'd like, but since it didn't markedly bother me, I'd call it a minor flaw.<br /><br />•It seems that <i>The False Prince</i> qualifies as <b>middle-grade</b>, but I wouldn't hesitate to recommend it to more mature readers. With the exception of Rick Riordan, I don't read middle-grade books and don't find particular pleasure in them, but I reckon that my enthusiasm for this book speaks for itself.<br /><br />➽ The reason you should read this is very, very simple: <b>Sage</b>. You don't need further motive. He is an <b>irresistible character</b> and an irresistible <b>narrator</b>, who knows what to withold and what to let on to increase our curiosity and our surprise. <b>Priceless</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="18181346252962882596" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1508811255" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7702505284852472312">I don't know how exactly to describe what I felt about this book but I'm certain that this one has captured my attention and my heart from the moment I turned the first page,'til the last! It was like,I had been magnetized by this book and couldn't let it out of my grip.(can't stay away from it,I even had to hold my bladder!Lol!)<br/><br/>This is a story of a 14 year old orphan boy named SAGE,(the protagonist here,who is so clever,strong,and with a witty-sharp tongue)who was bought by a royal regent named</span>
  <span id="freeText7702505284852472312" style="display:none">I don't know how exactly to describe what I felt about this book but I'm certain that this one has captured my attention and my heart from the moment I turned the first page,'til the last! It was like,I had been magnetized by this book and couldn't let it out of my grip.(can't stay away from it,I even had to hold my bladder!Lol!)<br /><br />This is a story of a 14 year old orphan boy named SAGE,(the protagonist here,who is so clever,strong,and with a witty-sharp tongue)who was bought by a royal regent named Bevin Connor,to be a part of a scheme of being an impostor(false)prince of a kingdom named Carthya.<br /><br />Along with Sage are three other orphans: Latamer,Tobias and Roden.Each one would compete for the prince's throne that revolves a fierce competition.And of course,I rooted for Sage the entire time because I just simply love him! What's not to love about this boy when he's everything you've wanted for a son?(when you're a mom like me,of course!) He is charming,smart,hilarious and witty! He maybe stubborn at times but he absolutely has a huge heart especially with orphans like him.<br /><br />This is my first book of Jennifer A.Nielsen and I instantly fell in love with her and with her novel. She did an incredibly clever job of creating this book by putting a lot of twists and turns,non-stop action,adventure and suspense through out the book.The characters were amazing,and each one played an important role in the story,uniquely.<br /><br />And though,I may have predicted the main twist or the over all plot,It was really fulfilling and justifying to see how things perfectly and wonderfully played out.<br /><br />I loved everything in this book because it's utterly irresistable! And the best part of this is the strong character development,and the story itself..that even when you would want more,this book can be a stand alone 'cause when you're done reading it,you'd feel happy and satisfied with the ending.(Yes,of course there's more to this series and I can't wait to read the next!)^^<br /><br />This is the best book I've read in a while,and I'm certain that this one would go to my "to be reread shelf"! This is a must read,highly recommended novel! Thanks to my wonderful friend,Muse-ic(SANDRA) for recommending this to me. You may also check PANG,MASOOMA,and ALAFIYA's review!^^</span>
