<div id="review_991056063" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/991056063" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/991056063?book_show_action=true">Jul 09, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=middle-grade-reader">middle-grade-reader</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=get-for-kids">get-for-kids</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer991056063" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11691658142392906390"><b>Warning: This is a middle-grade reader</b><br/><i>Not that there's anything wrong with that...</i><br/><br/>I'm mentioning the MGR thing, because I don't want someone to look at my four star review, and think this is a four star review for an adult book. Or even a young adult book.<br/>See, I actually didn't realize I was picking up a middle-grade reader, because it was classified as fantasy in my digital library. Still, no harm done since I'm always on the lookout for something the kids might like.<br/><br/>I gotta say, I was pretty i</span>
  <span id="freeText11691658142392906390" style="display:none"><b>Warning: This is a middle-grade reader</b><br /><i>Not that there's anything wrong with that...</i><br /><br />I'm mentioning the MGR thing, because I don't want someone to look at my four star review, and think this is a four star review for an adult book. Or even a young adult book.<br />See, I actually didn't realize I was picking up a middle-grade reader, because it was classified as fantasy in my digital library. Still, no harm done since I'm always on the lookout for something the kids might like.<br /><br />I gotta say, I was pretty impressed. <br />The plot had a good enough twist, even though I suspected it early on, that I was still second-guessing right up till the Big Reveal.<br /><br />It's about a cheeky boy named Sage, who gets plucked (<i>unwillingly</i>) out of an orphanage by a shady noble with a <b>plan</b>.<br /><i>
  <b>What's the plan, you ask?</b>
</i><br />Well. Let's take a look at the title, shall we?<br /><i><b>Ooooh. I'll bet I know what that shady noble wants him to do!</b><br />Or that's what I imagine you'll say, anyway.</i><br />And you're right!<br />This guy has bought (<i>because you can buy orphans in this book</i>) four different boys, in an attempt to turn one of them into The MISSING Prince. <br />One boy gets the ax right off the bat, and the other three are left to sorta duke it out. Whoever can turn themselves into the best 'imitation prince' wins. They each know that their <i>benefactor</i> isn't going to leave any witnesses alive to ruin his <b>plan</b>, so whoever doesn't get picked...<br /><i>*Kkkkkkkt*</i><br /><i>That's my knife across the throat sound, in case you were wondering.</i><br /><br />The violence was there, but it wasn't excessive, and it was done in an age-appropriate way. Which is kinda nice from a mom's point of view. <br />There's a crush-style romance, but (again) it's all age appropriate.<br />The best part? I didn't feel like I was reading a cookie-cutter children's story.<br />Strange friendships, unlikely betrayals, family secrets, and a nice little touch of revenge thrown in for good measure.<br />I'm going to continue this series, in the hopes that it might be something I'll end up buying for the kids!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_313250208" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313250208" />
    <a title="Vinaya" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya"><img alt="Vinaya" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1294127450p2/4687823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313250208?book_show_action=true">Apr 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vinaya" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vinaya" href="/user/show/4687823-vinaya">Vinaya</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=could-have-been-better">could-have-been-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=books-i-liked">books-i-liked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=i-coulda-done-it-better">i-coulda-done-it-better</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=cute-but-nothing-special">cute-but-nothing-special</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=ya-fantasy">ya-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4687823-vinaya?shelf=fluff-fluffy-fluffest">fluff-fluffy-fluffest</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313250208" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6868129625436556049">There is no way you can read The False Prince, and not have the inevitable comparisons to Megan Whalen Turner's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143163048' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Thief</a> crop up. Both are stories of young men, obscure nobodies charged with a greater purpose, subject to distrust and contempt and ridicule, involved in complicated matters far above their station. However, The Thief is, without doubt, the better man, so to speak. Unlike Gen, Sage, the protagonist of this story, is neither subtle, nor particularly clever. And neither is the story </span>
  <span id="freeText6868129625436556049" style="display:none">There is no way you can read The False Prince, and not have the inevitable comparisons to Megan Whalen Turner's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/143163048" rel="nofollow noopener">The Thief</a> crop up. Both are stories of young men, obscure nobodies charged with a greater purpose, subject to distrust and contempt and ridicule, involved in complicated matters far above their station. However, The Thief is, without doubt, the better man, so to speak. Unlike Gen, Sage, the protagonist of this story, is neither subtle, nor particularly clever. And neither is the story as a whole.<br /><br />This book was a fun romp, despite the heavy-handed hints and the reader being railroaded into a very obvious conclusion. However, like I said, it lacks the elegance of Turner's prose and pacing. The story is of Sage, an orphan boy who is picked up along with two other orphans by a twisted patriot, whose aim is to train one of the boys to take the place of a dead prince of a kingdom on the verge of civil war. Oh, and did I mention this training spans only two weeks? Yes, apparently, in two weeks, three orphan boys from the streets are expected to learn to read, write, dance, fight and comport themselves like royalty, and to do so with a flair that will fool an entire complement of watchful, vengeful courtiers. <br /><br />There are many, many flaws in this book, not the least its simplistic approach to plot and characterization. There is no attempt to paint in the shades of grey to any of the characters. Both Sage's actions and his rationalizations are pretty much out there, all the time. As are those of all the other characters. But the story flowed smoothly and fast, and despite knowing <i>exactly</i> what was going to happen, I still kind of enjoyed the journey. This is for people looking for a fast, uncomplicated read, or for the younger spectrum of YA fantasy readers. Nothing great, or even special, but cute enough in its own way. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6868129625436556049" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1353312250" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1353312250" />
    <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four"><img alt="Robin (Bridge Four)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473392517p2/14105531.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1353312250?book_show_action=true">Aug 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin (Bridge Four)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin (Bridge Four)" href="/user/show/14105531-robin-bridge-four">Robin (Bridge Four)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=awesome-audio">awesome-audio</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14105531-robin-bridge-four?shelf=fantastic-fantasy">fantastic-fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1353312250" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13704517772994940976">Seems like I can't say no to a buddy read with my pals at <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles' rel='nofollow noopener'>Buddies Books and Baubles</a>. What's another book tossed onto the pile? <br/><br/>Short review cuz I’m so behind on them….<br/><br/>Sage is a classic rapscallion, I don’t get to use that word enough, I mean when we meet him he is running through the city trying to keep a hold of a slippery roast he just stole. The kid has a quick tongue that always seems to get him into as much trouble as it gets him out of and he seems to have a little <s>problem</s> gift with sticky</span>
  <span id="freeText13704517772994940976" style="display:none">Seems like I can't say no to a buddy read with my pals at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148164-buddies-books-and-baubles" rel="nofollow noopener">Buddies Books and Baubles</a>. What's another book tossed onto the pile? <br><br>Short review cuz I’m so behind on them….<br><br>Sage is a classic rapscallion, I don’t get to use that word enough, I mean when we meet him he is running through the city trying to keep a hold of a slippery roast he just stole. The kid has a quick tongue that always seems to get him into as much trouble as it gets him out of and he seems to have a little <s>problem</s> gift with sticky fingers.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1438876444ra/15765463.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="theif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He seems like an industrious young orphan on the brink of being on his own until someone shows up and makes him an offer he literally can’t turn down. It seems like Sage will be in a competition with a few other boys, the prize is initially unclear but it soon becomes apparent that to lose would be very dangerous. So Sage must learn everything he can in two weeks or possibly not make it out of this situation alive<br><blockquote>
  <i>Master Graves was incensed and said, as punishment for my disruption, I would have to write my letters an extra ten times that day. <br>“Ten times the better I’ll know them, then,” I said. “How strange that you should punish me by ensuring I come out more educated than Roden, who has tried to obey you.”</i>
</blockquote><br>Middle Grade books are fun to read sometimes because I don’t have to put a ton of thought into them. This story is really readable. Sage and his discordant ways are easily likable and I enjoyed how he turned every obstacle into an advantage. He plays people off each other well and is as stubborn as a rock when he sets his mind on something no matter the consequences he must pay.<br><br>As an adult I guessed many of the twists that the book had coming in it. There were still a couple of surprises but not as many as there probably would have been if I was a younger reader. That didn’t stop it from being enjoyable though and I sped my way through the story very easily. <br><br>I didn’t only like Sage I also became attached to a few of the other characters like Hobb and Imogen. The friendships that Sage built with them along the way were some that I know will play out more in the upcoming books. There is a cute inkling of a romance with Imogen but it was totally age appropriate and it was refreshing to have something stay so innocent.<br><br>Even though this is a trilogy this first book wraps up nicely as a standalone.<br><br><b>Overall</b> - If you have kids and are looking for something to read with them that won’t bore you to tears. Or if you are like me and enjoy a good fun MG fantasy every now and again with interesting characters then this should be perfect for your needs.<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="13704517772994940976" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_304023280" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/304023280" />
    <a title="Elizabeth Drake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2230747-elizabeth-drake"><img alt="Elizabeth Drake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1271509716p2/2230747.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/304023280?book_show_action=true">Mar 31, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elizabeth Drake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elizabeth Drake" href="/user/show/2230747-elizabeth-drake">Elizabeth Drake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2230747-elizabeth-drake?shelf=2012-books">2012-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2230747-elizabeth-drake?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2230747-elizabeth-drake?shelf=top-books-in-2012">top-books-in-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer304023280" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1089408965109607081"><br/>This review can also be found on <a href='http://readingbetweenclasses.blogspot.com/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Reading Between Classes</a><br/><br/><b>Cover Impressions</b>: The cover doesn't stand out as much as I would like. It is simple and clean and I do like the gold crown and lettering on a blue background. <br/><br/><b>The Gist</b>: As an orphan running the streets of Carchar, Sage has learned to depend on his quick wits and quicker mouth to survive. When he finds himself one of four boys bought by a wealthy nobleman with a dastardly plan to gain control of the throne, Sage must use every trick at his </span>
  <span id="freeText1089408965109607081" style="display:none"><br />This review can also be found on <a href="http://readingbetweenclasses.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Reading Between Classes</a><br /><br /><b>Cover Impressions</b>: The cover doesn't stand out as much as I would like. It is simple and clean and I do like the gold crown and lettering on a blue background. <br /><br /><b>The Gist</b>: As an orphan running the streets of Carchar, Sage has learned to depend on his quick wits and quicker mouth to survive. When he finds himself one of four boys bought by a wealthy nobleman with a dastardly plan to gain control of the throne, Sage must use every trick at his disposal to outmaneuver the other boys and convince the kingdom that he is fit to rule.<br /><br /><b>Review</b>: The False Prince is the first book in The Ascendance Trilogy, and when I finished this book I was incredibly thankful that there are more to come while, at the same time, lamenting that I did not have the next installment NOW. This novel manages to invoke the same sense of intrigue and danger that Game of Thrones does, but presents it in a manner that is appropriate for a young audience. At the end I found myself warring contradicting emotions as half of me wanted to finish quickly so that I could find out what happens while the other half wanted to slow down a savor each word. <br /><br />The voice of Sage, hooked me from the very first page. He is clever, witty and self-deprecating. He interjects a wonderful sense humor into the most serious of situations and is able to manipulate the other characters into playing along in his grand master plan. His antics left me laughing, shaking my head or asking "why can you not keep your mouth shut!" (and sometimes all three) in the most wonderful of ways. Sage is the type of character that is impossible not to root for and I truly feel that he will appeal to both male and female readers, a feat that seems difficult to accomplish in most YA novels. <br /><br />The plot unfurls slowly but steadily, with secrets and betrayals around every corner. There was not a single moment when I was bored or wishing for more action. This is one of those books in which seemingly insignificant details will later be revealed as integral to the plot. I adore novels where all the puzzle pieces seem to fall into place, creating a finished piece that is full of detail and leaves the reader reflecting on all of the moments that brought us to this place. <br /><br />The False Prince is easily the best book I have read this year and I am especially excited because this is a book that I can hand both my male and female students knowing that they will return begging for the next in the series. This is a wonderful addition to any classroom library, kid's bookshelf or adult's to-be-read pile. <br /> <br /><b>Teaching/Parental Notes</b>:<br />Age: 12 and up<br />Gender: Both - Boys will LOVE this book!<br />Sex: None<br />Violence: Shooting with an arrow, swordplay, stabbing<br />Inappropriate Language: None<br />Substance Abuse: None</span>
  <a data-text-id="1089408965109607081" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Ages 14+ for mild violence</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Sarah Grace by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/47111982-mary">Mary</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=adult">adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=my-favorites">my-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/59507807-sarah-grace-grzy?shelf=i-own">i-own</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1859954153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7181658087900360073">Jennifer A. Nielson is the queen of her genre. The first book in the Ascendence Trilogy, <i>The False Prince</i>, is a perfect balance of plot twists, action, heart, wit, and emotion. I think I can honestly say this is the most complex book I have ever read. <br/><br/>Written in the first person POV of a fifteen-year-old orphan boy named Sage, Nielson masterfully reveals details to the reader one by one throughout the book, and just when you think you’ve got it figured out, the story takes another twist - then a</span>
  <span id="freeText7181658087900360073" style="display:none">Jennifer A. Nielson is the queen of her genre. The first book in the Ascendence Trilogy, <i>The False Prince</i>, is a perfect balance of plot twists, action, heart, wit, and emotion. I think I can honestly say this is the most complex book I have ever read. <br /><br />Written in the first person POV of a fifteen-year-old orphan boy named Sage, Nielson masterfully reveals details to the reader one by one throughout the book, and just when you think you’ve got it figured out, the story takes another twist - then another and another. <br /><br />Sage is a remarkably complex character. He’s arrogant and cocky, sarcastic, and incredibly smart, but he’s also insecure, unsure, and still a young boy trying to figure out how to survive in this dangerous world. The reader can’t help but empathize with at least one aspect of his character, if not more. <br />The rest of the cast is nearly as complex. From the manipulating Bevin Connor to the villainous Creegan, to the tenderhearted, but misled Mott, bookerly Tobias, and sweet Imogen. The entire cast of characters is vibrant and realistic and left me shaking my head in awe at their complexities. <br /><br />Not only is Nielson a master of characters, she is also extremely talented when it comes to description and world building. Within the course of one short book (these are YA novels, after all), she creates a brand new, large and multiplex world that is so vivid the reader isn’t just reading this story, they are <i>in</i> the story, living the story. The plot, in my opinion, is unparalleled in its uniqueness and intricacies. It’s hard to say much about it without spoiling anything due to the aforementioned numerous twists and turns, so we’ll just leave it at that. <br /><br />Overall, Neilson pens a novel that will grip your attention and your emotions from the very start, and won’t let go until you finish the entire trilogy. (I definitely recommend having all three on hand before starting The False Prince!) <br /><br /><br />Note: I highly recommend listening to Scholastic Inc’s audiobook version of the series narrated by Charlie McWade. He does an incredible job personifying each character.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7181658087900360073" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>,

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2917552821" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8825428539936449268"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “A person can be educated and still be stupid, and a wise man can have no education at all.” </i> </b><br/><br/>What an excellent fantasy middle grade novel! The False Prince is about Sage, who is rounded up from an orphanage with three other boys who all become enmeshed in a treasonous plot. The boys are not given much choice in the matter, they are to become impersonators of a prince, or they will be killed. Sage must use his wits to come out on top, all the while avoiding danger.<br/><br/><b> <i> “The saddest th</i></b></span>
  <span id="freeText8825428539936449268" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br /><br /><b> <i> “A person can be educated and still be stupid, and a wise man can have no education at all.” </i> </b><br /><br />What an excellent fantasy middle grade novel! The False Prince is about Sage, who is rounded up from an orphanage with three other boys who all become enmeshed in a treasonous plot. The boys are not given much choice in the matter, they are to become impersonators of a prince, or they will be killed. Sage must use his wits to come out on top, all the while avoiding danger.<br /><br /><b> <i> “The saddest thing is there won’t be anyone to miss us when we’re gone. No family, no friends, no one waiting at home.”<br />“It’s better that way,” I said. “It’ll be easier for me, knowing my death doesn’t add to anyone’s pain.”<br />“If you can’t give anyone pain, then you can’t give them joy either.” </i> </b><br /><br />I really enjoyed this book. It starts off a little bit slow, but what fantasy novel doesn’t? I was able to predict the largest twist, but there were many along the way I didn’t see coming. I loved seeing how everything unwinded and the result at the end of the book. I honestly cannot wait to listen to the second book, I think only good things came come from this story.<br /><br /><b> <i> “In a crowd of a thousand boys claiming to be the prince, there would be only one with the same look of trouble in his eye.” </i> </b></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8940023514676364746">This book was such a treat to read and I am so glad I started 2015 with it! I really enjoyed the characters and I just had a lot of fun while reading it. Although this book is located in the YA section in Barnes & Noble, I definitely think it has a middle grade feel to it. I think some readers will have problems with the lack of world building and the novel being rather predictable, but I was enjoying myself so much while reading it that these things didn't matter to me. Great characters, great </span>
  <span id="freeText8940023514676364746" style="display:none">This book was such a treat to read and I am so glad I started 2015 with it! I really enjoyed the characters and I just had a lot of fun while reading it. Although this book is located in the YA section in Barnes &amp; Noble, I definitely think it has a middle grade feel to it. I think some readers will have problems with the lack of world building and the novel being rather predictable, but I was enjoying myself so much while reading it that these things didn't matter to me. Great characters, great dialogue, so much fun!</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('eKMwJzi15Ym2TWMvHkPSuREVgLp+JaYDPQey68eMnJF7eBGtcbNmUN542HbMTi/RobY0mapgtIYUfqN6jf3d7A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gUcHhFzu/azglGGUg2aKHl5hPNJusYjZbGb+YyGSLN2CnCYOFeh+dYih2s1Ra3d27sKI8br0mlxFH+/ya+NtoA==')})
  }
